Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 233

— (Maode)

Mrs. Coolidge said: "The reason Americans are successful in doing things is because they are not afraid of failure, and whatever they have in mind to do, they will put their whole heart into it, go all out, and simply not think that there will be any failure. If there is a failure, they will immediately stand up, embrace an even greater determination, and strive forward until they succeed." This saying can be our motto.

"An inch of time is worth an inch of gold, but an inch of gold cannot buy an inch of time." This means that time is precious because other things, once lost, can be recovered. Only time, once a minute is lost, there is one minute less. Once a moment has passed, it is lost. Once lost, no matter what power you use, you can never recover it. But many people think that today has passed, there is still tomorrow, and the tomorrow of today, and the tomorrow of tomorrow. If you think so erroneously and throw away golden time, wouldn't it be a pity? Young people! Stop dreaming about the tomorrow of tomorrow. You must seize the present and do it. Otherwise, when your hair is white, it will be too late to regret.

Spring Boating on West Stream 234

— Lake Beggar

West Stream is known for its snow, and boating is enjoyed during the clear frost and hot maple leaves. If it is in the third month of spring, floating on a bay of misty water, there are few visitors. Because the place is secluded, unlike the hustle and bustle of West Lake with its carriages weaving through and the rolling yellow dust, I took a boat to explore it at my leisure. It was the busy season for farming, and the fields were full of plowing and mulberry cultivation. The misty villages were sparse, and who was living in leisure? At Hejia Wharf, I called for a ferry for some time before I got an old woman who agreed to go with a large fee. As the lone oar first released, seagulls dotted the water like snow. How could this scene be found on the Six Bridges? After several turns, the water country opened in seclusion. Emerging from the shore, the new trees were a mix of trees, all green and lush. Only a few cuckoos called to each other overhead. Further away, the fields were filled with lush green seedlings, and the mulberries were heavy and purple, all worthy of painting. Occasionally passing one or two fences, dogs barked in surprise. Scolding them, they followed the shore without stopping until the branch of the harbor stopped. The boat arrived at Jiaolu Nunnery, resting on the waterfront railing. The empty corridor was silent, with only fish and frogs communicating with each other. Lotus stalks in the pool were just emerging, and the green duckweed was not yet halfway there, so the fallen heads and temples in the water could still be clearly seen. Entering Fangshen Temple, a niche of incense and fire, worshiping the poetess, I often recall the endless waves and red sails. Further west is Qiuxue Nunnery. Leaning on the Finger-snapping Tower, gazing at the 30 acres of green reeds competing for emerald green, the vitality before me is so great, who knows that they will all turn white in autumn? As the sun sets and the clouds return, the shadows of people lie horizontally on the algae. Looking at the evening cooking in the distant lake, it is slowly rising up.

On Human Flavor 235

— Zhang Ke

To be a person, one must have a flavor that people appreciate. People's faces are different, and human flavors are also different.

The human flavor that is expressed on the outside is called body odor. This odor is different for everyone. If you are quiet and get used to it, you can always tell the difference. It can always be confirmed between husband and wife, because they are most used to each other. Smelling it is an odor, and it is rarely as fragrant as orchids throughout the ages, so it is called: body odor beauty! The name is beautiful, because it comes from the true source, even if it smells, it is also beautiful.

The human flavor that is stored inside is called addiction. People's addictions are different in elegance, vulgarity, evil, and righteousness. The beauty and ugliness of the strange and bizarre are endless. In short, each has its own flavor to find. Those who are similar can get together and those who are suppressed will be rejected. This is the truth of human nature, which is not necessarily unworthy of being called addiction beauty.

Indeed! Zhang Dai's "Record of Qi Zhixiang's Addiction" says: "People without addictions cannot be associated with, because they have no deep feelings; people without flaws cannot be associated with, because they have no true spirit. My friend Qi Zhixiang has an addiction to calligraphy and painting, an addiction to kicking football, an addiction to drums and bells, an addiction to ghost shows, an addiction to pear gardens..." Oh, what a thick human flavor this is!

If Zhang Xianzhong, people know that his addiction is killing people. The addiction is to kill and kill, which is his truth, and makes him feel cute!

If Gu Hongming, people say that his addiction is the smell of small feet. It is certainly an addiction to smell and smell, which is also his truth, and I also feel that he is cute!

Many of my compatriots are addicted to rolling cigarettes and opium! They are not ashamed to draw and draw on them, which is also true, and very cute! But some people boast about their precision and elaborate their shelves with laws that are not forbidden, while others embellish their words to reduce the amount and avoid them as deeply as possible, because the orders are strict. These are all self-deprecating their truth, and I don't think they are very cute!

There are different types of addictions: some like to eat scabs, and some like to defecate. The son of a certain Mr. in my neighborhood has been addicted to salt since he was a child. He would be lethargic and sick if he did not eat a few handfuls of salt every day, and he still does not give up when he grows up. A certain girl in my distant neighborhood, with a wonderful age and beautiful appearance, likes to chew the grass paper used for wiping dirt behind her back. All kinds of things can be compiled into a huge volume. These people are usually ashamed of being different from others, and although it is not very cute to avoid them, it is the norm, and they do not lose their addiction.

This is why the charter of a certain society does not prohibit addictions, nor does it advise people to quit smoking?

If the body has no odor, it is not far from death; if a person has no addictions, what is the difference between him and animals? Oh! Do these people lack human flavor? I greatly lament them!

Spendthrift Woman 236

— Hua Ling

Spendthrift Woman is a pitiful woman who was driven out of a large clan in our village. That was already thirteen years ago. The woman was originally the fourth young mistress of a certain room in this big family. Three years after she got married, her husband, the fourth young master, fell ill. After the fourth young master passed away, the four walls were bare. All that was left was a son who had just passed his first birthday. Her husband's brothers did not take care of themselves well, so naturally they did not take care of the fourth young mistress very much. At that time, the fourth young mistress was only twenty-one years old. Alone in an empty bedroom, the situation was bleak. Needless to say, the lives of the mother and son depended on the two piculs of rice from the charity village every year, which was naturally not enough. Because of the lack of food and sex, she had an affair with a tea merchant who came and went every spring and autumn, who lived across the street.

In a town of three or four hundred families, things the size of sesame seeds would be treated as news and rumors, let alone the fourth young mistress, who was the daughter-in-law of this big family, actually doing this kind of thing. Immediately, one told ten, and ten told hundreds. The tea houses and taverns all treated it as a novel thing to spread. This aroused the anger of the clan chief of this big family, who opened the ancestral hall and discussed it with the whole clan, driving her out of the ancestral hall and escorting her out of the country to protect the reputation of the whole clan. From then on, no one knew where the fourth young mistress was, and the tea merchant no longer came to this town to do business. All that was left was the bloodline of the fourth young master, raised by the second young mistress, and a nickname given to her by the clan, "Spendthrift Woman."

Time quickly passed for thirteen years. This spring, a woman was suddenly discovered sweeping and crying at the tomb of the fourth young master. Although she was a bit old, everyone still recognized her as the Spendthrift Woman who was driven out thirteen years ago. It turned out that after she was driven out, she lived with the tea merchant. Now that the tea merchant was dead, she received an inheritance of thirty to forty thousand yuan. Because she could not forget the old sword, she came to sweep the tomb. As soon as this news spread, it caused a sensation throughout the clan again. It is heard that someone has mediated, donating 10,000 yuan to the ancestral hall, not pursuing the past, and allowing her to restore her surname.

This scene seems comical, but there are many sour and spicy things hidden inside.

Respectfully Announcing to Those Suffering from Jaundice: I suffered from jaundice again this time, my whole body was yellow, and I went to many famous doctors for treatment, but it was ineffective. Thanks to a close friend who introduced me to Mr. Wang Xinnan of Yi Da North Goods Store, No. 131 Xian Gua Street, outside Xiaodongmen. He had herbal medicine at home to treat this disease. Mr. Wang generously gave it to me, and after taking it for a week, the disease was cured. During this period, I did not spend any money, and I am very grateful. Now, because Mr. Wang has the good deed of giving medicine to help the world, I hereby announce it to those suffering from the same disease. (Song Qing)

Hearing the Rooster Crow, Stop Dancing 238

A: "Hearing the rooster crow, stop dancing" is not fashionable nowadays.

B: Why?

A: Now the dance halls are singing and dancing all night, and it's almost over when the rooster crows. Isn't that "hearing the rooster crow, stop dancing"!

Phoenixes Replace Nests 239

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 2: Fragrant Grass and Beautiful Women, Subtle Waves, and New Posts; Moonlit Night in the Small Building, Good Dreams Begin to Warm

Meng Yue was filled with worries after hearing these words. She thought that even Lian Budong was poisoned by these talented men and beautiful women. Thinking like this, she was too lazy to go downstairs for dinner, so she just asked Xiao Ju to send a pot of pot rice soaked in boiling water upstairs, and a small plate of pickled cabbage, which was her dinner. After dinner, she read two pages of books under the lamp, but she couldn't calm down. By chance, she looked up and saw a glittering thing in the willows next to the wall, dazzling. At first glance, she couldn't help but be surprised, but after looking carefully, it was the moon on the sixteenth night, a round circle, that had been gushing out for a long time. Unlike other trees, willows do not have big leaves that can block the light. It was swaying in the wind, flashing and revealing part of the moon, which was a different kind of interest. Also, where the moon was directly facing, the willow branches looked like they were coated with a layer of gold paint, which was even more beautiful. Meng Lan first looked at it by chance, but now she found it interesting, so she extinguished the lamp on the table, then lay on the table and looked up at the sky, reciting old poems at random. Although the poems were recited casually, most of the sentences were sad, so she was very unhappy with the beautiful moon scene. She suddenly thought that the ancients said that women are good at feeling sad, but that is actually a mistake. Chinese women are oppressed by etiquette, and they can't do what they want to do, and they can't say what they want to say. Besides thinking alone, where is the second way? Zhang Litian invented the four words "melancholy for the rest of their lives" in his novel that failed to win the pair, which is really appropriate. It's a pity that I can't write novels. If I could write novels, I would definitely use the four words "melancholy for the rest of their lives" as the title and write an article about the pain of women. Thinking of this, she felt a burst of numbness on the back of her hand, and then she realized that she was crossing her hands and supporting her chin, looking at the sky in a daze, forgetting to press on the back of her hand. This was a bit tired, and she was too lazy to light the lamp, so she closed the door and went to bed in a daze. As soon as her head hit the pillow, she thought of the two tall willows, facing each other all day long, but she had never really gone to the tree to linger. Tomorrow, I'll get up early and visit the willow trees when there's no one in the vegetable garden. With this plan, she was standing under two big willow trees the next morning. Looking up at the willow tree, the highest top was densely layered with willow branches, and she could hardly see the sky. However, the sun was not very strong, but it looked like the moon. She recited the ancient people's poem, "The moon is on the top of the willow tree, and people will meet after dusk." Then she heard someone behind her say: "This is also a melancholy for the rest of her life, right?" Looking back, it was the boy she met in Yuhuatai? He was still holding a small branch of apricot blossom and nodded with a smile: "This flower is for you." (To be continued)

Traveling in the Arts

Chinese Under the Armored Train 240

— Lin Liqin

Vsevolod Ivanov is a highly acclaimed modern Soviet writer. Among his many works is a novel depicting a peasant guerrilla team attacking an armored train during the Great Revolution: "The Armored Train." It is considered his most outstanding representative work. In 1932, Turkish journalists and writers visited the Soviet literary world. During their second meeting with Gorky, Gorky responded to the request of the Turkish guests and specifically pointed out this "Armored Train" to introduce to them, praising it as a noteworthy modern Soviet literary work. The famous critic Professor Kogan also gave it honorable praise in his "Ten Great Years of Literature." This novel, which is recognized as outstanding, has been translated into almost every country in the world, and has also been adapted into a drama for the stage. In the Soviet Union, the director of "The Armored Train" was the great contemporary director Stanislavsky. During the Soviet Drama Festival of 1933—June 1st—10th—on the third night of national celebration, "The Armored Train" was performed at the world-famous Moscow "Art Grand Theater." The role of the peasant guerrilla chief of staff, Vershinin, was played by the great dramatist Kacbalov. The American "Pasadena Playhouse" has also performed it many times.

Here, firstly because "The Armored Train" is a world-famous literary work, and secondly because we Chinese, who have always been despised by foreigners, are given a superior position in this book thanks to the author; and also given the honorary title of "Chinese Dragon," we feel even more fortunate to have received unexpected favor. Among the many revolutionary warriors, there is actually such a brave and upright hero that Russians admire and are ashamed of—the Chinese Shen Fangwu. Although this is a fictional character of a friendly writer, we are constantly looking forward to whether our national character can actually reciprocate their friendly gift. Indeed, it breeds that general hope, so we should especially solemnly introduce this Chinese under the armored train:

Regarding the deeds of Shen Fangwu, according to the narration in the original book, we can briefly retell a little here: He—Shen Fangwu, was a Chinese worker who had gone to Russia to weave mats. Perhaps due to hard work and frugality, he had a wife, a house, and a field of sorghum and corn. Unfortunately, in one day, his estate and property were destroyed by the fire of Imperlaticism, and everything disappeared. He resented his enemies and therefore sympathized with the revolution—he joined the peasant guerrilla team and followed the big-nosed, thick-bearded Russian, Vershinin, as a scout under his command. When the "Polar" armored train No. 1469, commanded by Captain Nebylatzov, was ordered to go to Vladivostok to suppress the uprising that was about to break out in the city, the Chairman of the Revolutionary Committee, Pokrevalov, ordered Vershinin to lead his peasant guerrilla team to the railway line in Mokrenka River to intercept this armored train and block its progress. On Vershinin's side, since receiving this order, someone suggested demolishing the rails, but after considering the difficulty of repairing them with the current manpower, Vershinin changed it to seeking a volunteer to lie on the rails and let the wheels of the armored train run over his body. Then, according to the rules, the armored train would definitely stop, and the commander and driver on the train would definitely get out to inspect the dead body on the rails and prepare to make a report. After such a twist, the strategic interception would not only be easy to succeed, but perhaps the "Polar" armored train, which was the strongest in combat power, could be seized. Later, because no one was willing to let his flesh touch the steel wheels, the quartermaster Okolok was angry. He threw away the gun in his hand and fell on the rails. Although he struggled with the last bit of courage to offer his flesh and blood to the steel and sacrifice for the strategy; but the terror of death before death eventually made him tremble a little. At this serious and tense moment, our Chinese Shen Fangwu, who had been very calm since the march, sprang up. He felt that it was cowardly and shameful for Okolok to lie on the rails and ask the peasants for vodka, so he ran over with a sneer and lay beside Okolok. As Okolok quietly left the rails with a guilty smile, the revolutionary passion, burning like a flame, further strengthened his determination to sacrifice. Before the "Polar" armored train No. 1469 arrived, he first raised his pistol and fired a shot at the back of his head, and then lay hard on the rails waiting for the rumbling of the wheels. As a result, Vershinin won the battle of hitting the train, the uprising in Vladivostok broke out, and the final victory belonged to our "Chinese under the armored train."

If Ivanov's "Armored Train" can be regarded as a true and accurate history, then in the history of the Soviet revolutionary war, our Chinese Shen Fangwu, perhaps, cannot be regarded as a dazzling superstar. If we turn back and unfold our own history of the Chinese revolutionary war: from Dr. Sun Yat-sen's organization of the "Revive China Society" and the advocacy of justice, to the Battle of Huanghuagang, to the Wuchang Uprising; as well as several great and tragic bloody battles in the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, and the glorious war of "January 28th" which is worth singing and weeping about, during this period, those equivalent to "the Chinese Shen Fangwu under the armored train" will be countless brave and upright heroes that Russians admire and are ashamed of. However, the seeds of honor are striving, and the back of boasting may be encouragement; rise up, Chinese under the armored train! The remaining pages of history are waiting for brilliant records.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Ten Thousand Miles of Fragrance 241

— Special

A few days ago, some friends went to Beiping for a trip. When they returned, I asked them about their impressions and feelings of the trip. They said that there were over two hundred of them, and they were just skimming the surface every day, like following an old woman to a wedding banquet, and they didn't get any impressions or feelings at all. However, they felt that the remnants of feudal ideology still filled the air of the old capital. Besides, they avoided talking about politics, as if there was an invisible and vicious force shrouding everyone's minds, suffocating their chests.

However, there is one thing I must tell you. After traveling during the day, we rested in our residence. The attendant asked, "Gentlemen, would you like to smoke opium?" I was surprised and asked, "Is opium not prohibited here at all?" The attendant replied, "No, it is forbidden elsewhere. But if you go to Ten Thousand Miles of Fragrance in Stone Hutong, there will be no problem." At first, I didn't understand what he meant, so I went with a friend. Upon entering, I saw a man with a small mustache behind the counter, sitting there sternly. Then I understood why there was no problem smoking opium there.

Entering the room, there were no fewer than seventy or eighty opium couches, and the business was very prosperous. Swallowing clouds and spitting fog, the room was filled with poisonous fumes. We didn't have opium addiction, but we just wanted to pass the time and witness the newly emerged miracle of Beiping. After it was over, the attendant said, "How was it? In the past, as long as a certain prince or lord supported something in Beiping, nothing would go wrong. Now, as long as the man with the small mustache supports something, anything that violates the law can be done. The organization and capital of Ten Thousand Miles of Fragrance do not belong to the man with the small mustache. He is just their shield. Now, as long as the man with the small mustache appears, nothing will happen." Hearing this, I couldn't help but sigh.

I heard that in the north, the man with the small mustache sells drugs, organizes gambling and takes a cut, and extorts money from the people, which has become their proper profession. I think fundamentally, it is our own fault. If they sell drugs, and we don't use their drugs, then they can't do anything. If they organize gambling and take a cut, and we don't want to get rich, they can't do anything. Now, they are engaged in illegal business, and their business is booming. In the final analysis, it is mostly our own fault. This is one point. Besides, there are also some traitors and lackeys who only seek profit and act as accomplices, using the man with the small mustache as a signboard to implement policies of suicide and self-destruction. The reason why our country cannot be saved lies in this.

For example, in the recent smuggling, if the people of our country had a little conscience, it would be very easy to prohibit this kind of smuggled goods. As long as merchants don't sell it for them, and the people don't buy it, then even if they smuggle, there is no way to smuggle. The method of resistance is very simple. However, merchants are blinded by profit, and the people don't know how to love their country, so the affairs of our country are getting worse and worse. Now, to stop it, we want to use conscience to restrain it, but conscience is no longer reliable. We want to use the law to restrain it, but the national law is also beyond reach. Is there really no way to deal with this? Or is there a way, but we are carefully considering it and unwilling to use it?

Alas, when I hear the three words "Ten Thousand Miles of Fragrance," I can't help but feel horrified, astonished, and surprised!

On the Wilderness 242

— Li Quanwen

Moonlit night, no wind, silvery liquid covers the entire Rabi wilderness.

The wilderness is vast and flat, stretching endlessly into the darkness in the distance. No sheds, no shadows of trees, no fields can be seen, only a patch of green pasture reveals the only wealth here.

We lightly whip, the horses trample forward on the rugged mud road dried after the rain. The unrhythmic sound of the wheels, the occasional snoring of the pigs on the cart, and our sporadic conversations monotonously break the silence of the wilderness.

We are regulars of the wilderness: every ten days we have to set off in the middle of the night, and trample across this wilderness to the market in the town dozens of miles away.

At first, this was a job that I hated and regretted, but I quickly got used to it; to the point that in the lonely journey, often without companions, I would quietly use meditation and the scenery of the night to adjust myself.

This time my companion was a Batavian man who grew vegetables. We met at a fork in the road just as we were about to enter this wilderness. Although we were strangers, we had the common habit of those who went to the market: the sympathy born out of the remote and lonely night journey quickly connected us into one. He was the tenant of two acres of land, a melancholy middle-aged man, who spoke very little, and every word he uttered was tinged with deep sadness. However, it was easy to see that he also had a hope, and even eagerly guarded the burning of that hope. Although the growth of that hope was only irrigated by sadness.

I am a nervous person who is easily moved and has an excessive amount of feelings, and his sadness quickly soaked through me involuntarily; in the sad meditation, I unconsciously and slowly floated up past struggles and future anxieties.

"This world"! I thought, and couldn't help but sigh.

"Uncle (Note 1), it must be hard for you?"

"What hardships do we have to feel? This world: alas, we were originally weeds grown out of bitterness!"

I gently raised the whip in the air and waved it, making a crisp cracking sound: occasionally the pigs on the cart also spewed out vague groans like snorts in their sleep, but immediately the deathly silence enveloped the surroundings again, leaving the sound of the wheels mechanically spreading to all directions.

I re-buried myself in contemplation, and sighs and resentment under the trampling of the iron hooves of the oppressive nation. …

"Uncle!" My companion suddenly woke up the sleeping silence and my thoughts. "Do you think we will have a day to stand up"?

"Oh! Even solid walls have their collapse, one day when our strength is enough, we will be able to climb the ladder!"

"But, uncle, …"

"Weak nations have gradually opened their eyes under the dazzling sunlight; have you heard that a prairie fire can be quieted with water from buckets?"

"But! Um, at what time? Uncle, what do you think?"

"Maybe the day after tomorrow, maybe there will always be a time when we can climb the ladder!"

"That's what I think, uncle!"

My companion's horse suddenly raised its nasal voice and screamed sharply, and my gray horse followed with its long scream that seemed to be rolling its tongue in its nose; this scream first rolled in the nearby air, slowly drifted in all directions in the wilderness and finally disappeared into the boundless darkness in the distance; but it seemed that there was still a faint echo bouncing back from a distance, still lingering in my ears.

"That year: we succeeded and then!"

My companion muttered sadly; shaking the whip in his hand again and again in the air, but never swung it even once.

"That was a good bomb; didn't your compatriots wake up a lot because of it?"

"But, uncle, the prevention is even more severe!"

"The dike cannot regulate the turbulent flood, and the fence cannot stop the flying birds! You know!"

"However, those immersed in numbness are as many as flies! Uncle."

"A lump of ice will slowly dissolve when it falls into hot water! Who has ever seen a painting that is colored well in one go?"

"Ah! Uncle! You think the same as me! Really came out of one brain!"

"……"

Page 20

The pig spat out its vague ramblings again: a lower place on the road made my car vibrate slightly more violently.

"There will always be a time when we can climb the ladder, there will always be that day!"

My companion sighed a long breath, and when he said the word "day" at the end, he waved the whip in the air several times more forcefully: the sharp cracking sound startled his horse and made it run a few steps faster.

While speaking, the wheels followed the road and turned a large bend on the wilderness. The road back formed a very neat right angle on the right.

The wilderness returned to silence as before. We were all silent, each jumped into the pond of contemplation, silently letting the wheels break the boundless silence with its unrhythmic sound and carry us into the darkness in the distance. …

Note 1: Locals in the Dutch East Indies call Chinese people "Uncle."

Note 2: That is the year of the National Party Revolutionary Uprising of the Dutch East Indies natives on November 12, 1926.

The Village Chief's Home 243

— Lin Jia

Before dinner, in the dim twilight, a thin, tall man rudely walked into the house. I recognized him at a glance. He was Mou San's son from the West Village, the gatekeeper and gunman who had been hired in our village two years ago. It was said that he had been making a living at home by fishing and hunting wild birds for the past two years. He looked a little more haggard, dark, and thin than when he was a gatekeeper. It seemed that the world had given him a lot of wind, frost, and torture in the past two years.

His father was the village chief. At this time, he was wearing a civil servant uniform, leaning obliquely on the kang, smoking a long pipe. The man sat uncomfortably on the edge of the kang. After answering a few questions from others absentmindedly, he said solemnly and unnaturally:

"Village Chief, I have been implicated by Cheng Wang?"

The whole room was silent for a moment. We were all very familiar with Cheng Wang's case. He was a murderer who caused a stir in the area for the sake of money. Just a few days ago, he was tied up with his bloody clothes and led to the city.

The father slowly exhaled a long stream of smoke from the left corner of his mouth, and said without expression:

"How did you know?"

"Today, the village chief from that village went to my house and said: 'Someone, Cheng Wang has implicated you. If you don't want to be involved in the case, you have to have a plan not to be involved!'—He first came with such a big scare, and then whispered sneakily: 'I think you should run away. Ask your grandpa to take out some money, and I will take care of things for you.'"

He was a little out of breath. After a slight pause, he said more excitedly:

"Village Chief, what do you think he is saying! Isn't this just framing me? Why should I run? Where should I run? I haven't committed any crime out of thin air..."

The father remained silent, which made the man a little embarrassed. He quietly changed his breath and said again:

"I came here specifically to ask what's going on? To get guidance from the village chief, what should I do about this?"

The father rolled his eyelids at him, as if putting him on a scale to weigh him, and said:

"Are you really innocent?"

He stood up all of a sudden:

"Village Chief, I am naturally innocent. I have been hired in this village. You can't say you don't know my temper. I am poor, but I am honest. I can't do things like killing people for money."

The father said again so calmly:

"It's good if you're really innocent. But when a thief bites, it goes in three inches deep. You have to admit you're unlucky."

When he was about to leave, a long-term worker was wrapping a package of gunpowder. He said casually:

"What? Gunpowder?"

"Yeah, I got a wild duck today, but I missed it!" The long-term worker said very proudly.

"That stuff is nothing rare. In a few days, I will catch a few and send them over."

Saying that, he walked out with sparse footsteps.

After he left, the father tapped the edge of the kang with the bowl of his pipe and said:

"Not a good thing either, unreliable!"

I said: "The village chief is not good either, he wants to rip him off."

The father's lips moved, but he didn't speak.

The next evening, I was reading a book in the house by the light of the paper window, when suddenly I heard my mother shouting in the yard:

"Ka, come and see, Mou Dasheng brought some wild ducks!"

I ran out and saw the man standing on the platform, a long shotgun leaning against the brick wall next to the door, two pairs of beautiful wild ducks curled up at his feet, my mother was bending over, smiling and examining them.

The mother said:

"This thing is really beautiful, so lifelike, how can I eat it! Can't I keep it?"

"Oh, I can't even eat it," he laughed unnaturally. "Madam, please stir-fry and eat it quickly, this thing is very fragrant, even better than chicken. When I catch some that are in good condition, I will send them over to keep, these are all broken."

Two pairs of little things, crawling restlessly on the ground, with green, light yellow, and silver-white feathers combining into beautiful patterns. Flat and long beaks, curved necks, forming a novel shape. On one of the wings, bright red blood was oozing. I was dominated by a feeling of liking and pity.

In order to understand the mood of this man who hunted birds all year round, I shifted my gaze to this man's face, his dark, dry, haggard face was half-raised, and he was distractedly lost in thought in the spring breeze of the evening. I suddenly remembered his thoughts last night, as if suddenly struck by an inexplicable blow.

I silently retreated back into the house, and heard him nagging to his mother about what he had discussed last night.

Oyuya (Hot Bath House) 244

— Lei Shiyu

——Etchings of Tokyo——

This is a bathhouse. The storefront also has cloth curtains like those of "yakitori" shops, but these cloth curtains are clean, although the cloth is mostly the same light blue. The words diagonally arranged on these cloth curtains are also particularly large, and the two words before and after (the "O" and "ya" characters) are also written in Roman letters. However, even without that sign, you wouldn't mistake it for a food business. Because the door is very spacious and clean, especially the roof is high and towering. At the same time, at 11:00 AM, especially after 5:00 or 6:00 PM, if you walk past the door or from the side, the sound of wooden basins and hard earthen floors hitting each other, like striking a wooden fish, will be transmitted to your ears, sometimes loud and sometimes soft.

If you are a newcomer, and if you have a shy heart that respects yourself, when you walk through that main hall door, please be sure to look up at the two entrances and determine the direction you should go by reading the words "male" or "female" written above them. At the entrance, there are one or two men or women greeting you, putting the wooden clogs you take off (boots are the same) on the rack next to them, and first giving you a wooden tag in the shape of a "Great Sword" brand cigarette with a number written on it. When you leave, you can use it to claim all your belongings. Once inside, located in the front center of the two scenes, there is a high platform, on which sits a male or female boss. In addition to receiving your "five cents" entrance fee or keeping any valuables you deposit, they always sit idly, looking at the men in this scene or the women in that scene. At most, when you come in, they will say: "Irasshai!" (Welcome!) When you leave, they will say: "Arigato!" (Thank you!)

After you give the money and step onto the floor paved with tatami mats, a girl will greet you and bring the rattan basket (you can take it yourself) to you to take off your clothes. Then you take your own towel and soap and walk into the bathhouse naked. There are wooden basins there, and many hot and cold water taps extend from the wall, so you will make the wooden basin and the water taps do whatever action. You can pour warm water directly on your body basin by basin, and then you can soak as much as possible in the hot water tank inside, no matter how much sweat flows down your forehead and face like a waterfall. It is said that letting it flow a lot is the most hygienic. When you think you are satisfied, then you step out of the tank and go straight to the previous location to do your bathing work. If you are reluctant to part with the hot water in the tank, no one will interfere if you soak a few more times. If you want to be more carefree, you can also. There are people inside who specialize in pounding your back. It is said that you have to give five more cents to give you this carefree feeling.

"Mr. Wang's Adventures" Production Log 250

— A True Record by Bai Yun

(May 2nd) Ye Qianyu came to Shanghai from Beijing to discuss the copyright issue with Shao Cunren.

(May 3rd) Zuo Ming and Ye Qianyu discussed the "Mr. Wang" script at Yingcun.

(May 5th) Ye Qianyu joined Tianyi as the producer of "Mr. Wang," with Zuo Ming as the screenwriter and director. The contract was signed, and Ye returned to Beijing that evening.

(May 6th) Xu Wei, a former New Era set designer, officially joined Tianyi.

(May 7th) Tianyi held a script meeting for "Mr. Wang."

(May 8th) The first draft of the "Mr. Wang's Adventures" script was completed.

(May 9th) Zuo Ming, Sang Shuzhen, and Zhai Qiqi discussed the casting for "Mr. Wang" at Guanshengyuan, planning to solicit actors for "Mr. Wang" and "Little A Yuan."

(May 10th) The first draft of the "Mr. Wang's Adventures" script was sent to Beijing for review.

(May 11th) Ye Qianyu sent a quick mail, with detailed colored drawings of "Mr. Wang's" costume.

(May 12th) Sang Shuzhen officially joined Tianyi to play Mrs. Wang, Mr. Wang's wife.

(May 13th) Shao Cunren, Gao Lihen, Zuo Ming, Leng Bo, and others discussed the plot of "Mr. Wang" again.

(May 14th) Zhu Xuehua, Shen Fu, and two others were hired as special screenwriters.

(May 15th) Xu Wei designed the costumes, and the initial review of "Mr. Wang" passed.

(May 16th) Zuo Ming, Zhu Xuehua, Shen Fu, Huang Miaozi, Gao Lihen, and others studied the "Mr. Wang" script in detail at Guanle on Avenue Joffre.

(May 17th) Zuo Ming rushed to write the second draft of the script, and Zhai Qiqi joined Tianyi.

(May 18th) Shen Fu agreed to write the script for "Mr. Wang's Way to Make Money."

(May 19th) Zuo Ming, Zhu Xuehua, and Huang Miaozi discussed the plot at Xinya.

(May 20th) The second draft of the "Mr. Wang's Adventures" script was sent to Beijing for review today.

(May 21st) The choice of actor for "Mr. Wang" is still undecided, and rumors of Zhu Shaoshaoquan are inaccurate.

(May 22nd) Shen Xin and two other newspapers published advertisements soliciting actors for "Mr. Wang" in "Mr. Wang" and "Little A Yuan."

Xu Jingang 251

Xu Xinfu's "Diamond," has been filming very hard these past few days. The stars and colleagues have given Xu Xinfu another name, "Xu Jingang", with the meaning derived from the "Jingang" in "Diamond".

Yesterday in "Diamond" a scene – a stage scene, was of an entertainment gathering held by an orphanage to examine funds. The Gu sisters, Lanjun and Meijun, starred, and several hundred temporary spectators were invited. Logically, watching female stars perform on stage should require purchasing tickets out of one's own pocket, but in fact, these hundreds of spectators not only watched the play for free, but each received a salary of one yuan, plus a free lunch. Moreover, the Gu sisters performed very seriously, no wonder once the scene was over, cheers thundered, and hundreds of different faces were filled with intoxicating spring breeze.

Shanghai Light Semi-Monthly Publication Today 252

The Shanghai Light Semi-Monthly, published by Shanghai Light Publishing House at No. 6, Yude Lane, East Tangjia Lane, is unique in content and innovative in subject matter. The writers are all famous authors. The content specializes in movies, volcanoes, literature and art, children's paradise, drama, the singing world, universities, photographs, illustrations, cartoons, and comic strips, totaling more than forty frames, and more than fifty articles. The cover is printed in three-color copperplate on glossy paper. The general agency is located at the Shanghai Dagongbao Agency Department, Shanghai Life Bookstore, and Shanghai Magazine Company. The annual subscription of thirty-six issues costs only one yuan and two dimes. All newsstands sell them for five cents each.
